  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2d3b12af-ff7f-493b-9652-05d3facdd34d'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer14290754123821908139">Humanity is all but extinguished after a war with Partials—engineered organic beings identical to humans—has decimated the population. Reduced to only tens of thousands by a weaponized virus to which only a fraction of humanity is immune, the survivors in North America have huddled together on Long Island. But sixteen-year-old Kira is determined to find a solution. As she </span>
  <span id="freeText14290754123821908139" style="display:none">Humanity is all but extinguished after a war with Partials—engineered organic beings identical to humans—has decimated the population. Reduced to only tens of thousands by a weaponized virus to which only a fraction of humanity is immune, the survivors in North America have huddled together on Long Island. But sixteen-year-old Kira is determined to find a solution. As she tries desperately to save what is left of her race, she discovers that that the survival of both humans and Partials rests in her attempts to answer questions about the war's origin that she never knew to ask.<br /><br />Playing on our curiosity of and fascination with the complete collapse of civilization, <em>Partials</em> is, at its heart, a story of survival, one that explores the individual narratives and complex relationships of those left behind, both humans and Partials alike—and of the way in which the concept of what is right and wrong in this world is greatly dependent on one's own point of view.<br /><br />Supports the Common Core State Standards.</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=dystopian-post-apocalyptic-utopian">dystopian-post-apocalyptic-utopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2012-favorites">2012-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer233658570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9202396975131268360">It seems as though YA Science Fiction is experiencing a bit of a resurgence lately. Like many other readers, I'm a little tired of the barely-dystopian trend, so it's great to see a very firmly science-oriented book like <i>Partials</i> come along. Airborne viruses + survivalist action drama + human interest story is a great combination, and one I think most fans of post-apocalyptic thrillers will enjoy. <br/><br/>In the year 2076, 11 years after an airborne viral outbreak, the average newborn lives just 56 hour</span>
  <span id="freeText9202396975131268360" style="display:none">It seems as though YA Science Fiction is experiencing a bit of a resurgence lately. Like many other readers, I'm a little tired of the barely-dystopian trend, so it's great to see a very firmly science-oriented book like <i>Partials</i> come along. Airborne viruses + survivalist action drama + human interest story is a great combination, and one I think most fans of post-apocalyptic thrillers will enjoy. <br /><br />In the year 2076, 11 years after an airborne viral outbreak, the average newborn lives just 56 hours. 16-year-old Kira Walker, a young medic interning at a hospital, thinks that the key to human survival lies in studying Partials, a group of rogue cyborgs described as "unthinking, unfeeling human killers." Since Partials released the virus to begin with, surely they have the answers to a cure--whether it's through their genetic makeup or through their knowledge. When her friend Madison gets pregnant, Kira embarks on a dangerous mission: to find and capture a Partial so she can save her friend's child.<br /><br />But you've seen some positive reviews and some negative ones, right? <b>So here is the type of person that I think will have a blast with this book.</b><br /><br /><b>You're a Battlestar Galactica fan.</b> There are many similar BSG elements in this book, in a very good way. Partials are very similar to Cylons, and there's a war between humans and Partials that will decide the fate of both. There are also some elements of Star Trek: TNG, and The Matrix in this book, which aren't bad influences to have at all. But lest you be concerned about knockoffs, this is definitely an original story, told in a very engaging way.<br /><br /><b>You like medical thrillers.</b> Kira runs a lot of tests on a captured Partial in this book, and while some readers may have an issue with all the medical business that goes on, I personally love books about viruses and analyses of scientific data, etc., so I very much enjoyed all that. Do Kira's experiments require some suspension of disbelief? Sure. Especially since a. she's a student b. we don't get all the answers we might be asking and c. this disease doesn't actually exist. (True story!) But what worked for me was that the author did a great job of walking us through the steps and logic and reasoning behind Kira's methodology.<br /><br /><b>Post-apocalyptic books rock your socks.</b> Something about this book reminded me a lot of the feel of Mira Grant's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7094569.Feed__Newsflesh_Trilogy__1_" title="Feed (Newsflesh Trilogy #1) by Mira Grant" rel="nofollow noopener">Feed</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8429687.Deadline__Newsflesh_Trilogy___2_" title="Deadline (Newsflesh Trilogy, #2) by Mira Grant" rel="nofollow noopener">Deadline</a>, but for the YA crowd--and I don't make those comparisons lightly. There is a great blend of virological talk, exciting action sequences, and entertaining twists and turns that will appeal to fans of the Newsflesh series. Plus there are some survivalist elements I also really enjoyed. Worrying about energy conservation, day to day needs, salvage runs? Please, tell me more!<br /><br /><b>You appreciate butt-kicking heroines.</b> I really liked Kira, who is a smart, responsible heroine, even if she is a little too narrowly focused on her ideals and a little too quick to fly off the handle. I would liked to have felt more of an emotional connection with her, the way I did with the very intriguing Samm <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[who is SO much more interesting than the sweet but frustrating Marcus <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but I did feel as though I understood her. And it's great to have a girl scientist portrayed in YA.<br /><br />Do any of these sound like you? If so, get thee to a bookstore and grab a copy of <i>Partials</i> asap!<br /><br />I will say that some of the secondary teen characters blended together for me, so that it wasn't until significant things happened to them that I remembered who was who and what part they were playing in the story. All the adults are there primarily to advance the plot as well, and basically serve as foils and obstacles to the teens. And even though it's understandable that teenagers have taken on more advanced roles earlier on due to the outbreak, they have such huge responsibilities that it does make you raise an eyebrow a bit; it's almost as if <i>Partials</i> was written with adult characters, but was adapted for the YA market. While some of the specifics of the story may strain credulity when you stop to look at the big picture, I have to admit that during reading, it's hard to care, because the story is so well-paced and entertaining. I'm hoping that in the sequel, we'll see deeper character development and further exploration of the ramifications of the Hope Act as the story continues.<br /><br />All in all, <i>Partials</i> was a lot of fun for me. My immediate reaction when I finished the book was "fan-freaking-tastic!" and I'm excited that there's such a great science fiction option out there for YA readers. Don't get me wrong, I love fluffy novels or the types of books that feature girls in pretty ballgowns. But I like the kind of girl who wears lab coats, doesn't mind risking her life for what she believes is right, and argues passionately about the civil rights of cyborgs, too.<br /><br /><i>This review also appears in <a href="http://backinthemidnightgarden.blogspot.com/2012/03/review-partials.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a>. An advance copy was provided by the publisher.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9202396975131268360" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271177449?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=dystopia-utopia">dystopia-utopia</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271177449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4792392321090481686">There was a serious lack of drama, suspense and tension in this book. The lengthy descriptions and idle conversations were dull enough without the subject matter going from hockey to guns to bombs. I braved the first boring 200 pages because I was sure once the hunt for the Partials began we would see something a little more kickass, dangerous, pulse-pounding... something that would make me excited to read on. Unfortunately, I was wrong. This is another one of those books that will be just right</span>
  <span id="freeText4792392321090481686" style="display:none">There was a serious lack of drama, suspense and tension in this book. The lengthy descriptions and idle conversations were dull enough without the subject matter going from hockey to guns to bombs. I braved the first boring 200 pages because I was sure once the hunt for the Partials began we would see something a little more kickass, dangerous, pulse-pounding... something that would make me excited to read on. Unfortunately, I was wrong. This is another one of those books that will be just right for fans of very slow plot development, but not one for people like me who prefer something a bit faster-paced and nastier.<br /><br />This story is about a world where the human population has dwindled to approx. 40,000 because of a disastrous war with genetically engineered soldiers called Partials. The remaining few have congregated on an island, but all the babies born to the women die within a few days due to the release of a virus by the Partials. The adults, however, remain immune to this virus. Now the thing I find quite unbelievable is that we're expected to just accept that expert researchers have been studying the babies for years in search of a cure, and yet it takes a sixteen year old girl to come up the idea that they should also be looking at why adults have immunity to the virus. I mean... duh.<br /><br />The romance, too, was so flat and uninteresting that it only served to make things worse. This book is for someone, I'm sure, though I don't know who to recommend it to. Probably those who thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11378763.The_Book_of_Blood_and_Shadow" title="The Book of Blood and Shadow by Robin Wasserman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book of Blood and Shadow</a> had good pacing.</span>

<div id="review_231921912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/231921912" />
    <a title="Lyndsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4224396-lyndsey"><img alt="Lyndsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1288890060p2/4224396.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/231921912?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lyndsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lyndsey" href="/user/show/4224396-lyndsey">Lyndsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=pov-primarily-female">pov-primarily-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=about-racially-diverse-cast-or-mcs">about-racially-diverse-cast-or-mcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=3rd-person-limited">3rd-person-limited</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=about-ai-robots-cybernetics">about-ai-robots-cybernetics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=about-post-apocalyptic">about-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=about-viruses-disease-plagues">about-viruses-disease-plagues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=about-pregnancy">about-pregnancy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=2012-upcoming">2012-upcoming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4224396-lyndsey?shelf=pacing-moderate">pacing-moderate</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231921912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13647369130425585867">You can now check out the Partials trailer right <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/videos/show/19827-partials-trailer' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a> on Goodreads!<br/><br/><u>
  <b>A Partials-themed Acrostic!</b>
</u><br/><br/><b>P</b>regnancy obligations for the young like in Bumped.<br/><br/><b>A</b>mateur military of Falling Skies.<br/><br/><b>R</b>ioters and mercenaries threaten way of life like in The Survivors.<br/><br/><b>T</b>he MC is a bad-ass female scientist like in Bones<br/><br/><b>I</b>nfertility woes of the women on the Lost island.<br/><br/><b>A</b>rtificially created humans similar to Cylons from Battlestar Galactica.<br/><br/><b>L</b>ots of myths being busted.<br/><br/><b>S</b>CIENCE!!! <u>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <b>The Rundown</b>
</u><br/> <br/>The world has be</span>
  <span id="freeText13647369130425585867" style="display:none">You can now check out the Partials trailer right <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/videos/show/19827-partials-trailer" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a> on Goodreads!<br><br><u>
  <b>A Partials-themed Acrostic!</b>
</u><br><br><b>P</b>regnancy obligations for the young like in Bumped.<br><br><b>A</b>mateur military of Falling Skies.<br><br><b>R</b>ioters and mercenaries threaten way of life like in The Survivors.<br><br><b>T</b>he MC is a bad-ass female scientist like in Bones<br><br><b>I</b>nfertility woes of the women on the Lost island.<br><br><b>A</b>rtificially created humans similar to Cylons from Battlestar Galactica.<br><br><b>L</b>ots of myths being busted.<br><br><b>S</b>CIENCE!!! <u>
  <br>
  <br>
  <br>
  <b>The Rundown</b>
</u><br> <br>The world has been decimated by an airborne virus that killed 99.9% of the population. The virus was released by beings called Partials, genetically engineered soldiers that look just like us but with 10 times the strength and stamina.<br><br>The Partials have let the few remaining humans live in peace as long as they don't cross the border into Partials territory. Every female of age is required to be pregnant as often and as soon as possible. The current reigning government, the Senate, figures that if the citizens have enough babies, some of them will eventually be born with a natural immunity to the airborne virus that fills the air around them and decimates their newborn population. After a decade of births, this still has not happened. Every baby dies within mere hours.<br> <br>Our main character, Kira, has this brilliant idea that the scientists should focus on discovering how the immunity really works and figure out why the remaining adults and the Partials are immune.<br><br><i>And now for an intermission of Lyndsey Thoughts:<br>Me: Wait a tic - <i>Kira</i> thinks of this?! No one else in a decade, not even the Senate, has thought of that?<br>Other Me: Duh, Lyndsey. She's the main character. <i>Of course</i>, she thought of it!<br>Me: Right. I guess she's pretty smart then.<br>Other Me: Also, the Senate is full of bozos.<br>Me: Okay, thanks for clearing that up, Self.</i><br><br>In order to investigate the Partials immunity, they need to find one that will help them and the chances of that are pretty much zero. So they have get a hold of one <i>somehow</i>. Here's where it gets interesting! Veddy, veddy interesting!!<br><br><b>
  <u>The Enevitable BSG Comparison</u>
</b><br><br>At first, I expected to be comparing this to Battlestar Galactic as I read. And sure, the storyline and background of the two share a lot of similarities, but Partials and BSG are two completely different beasts. I was completely caught up in the science and the questions of this book. Battlestar Galactica is so epicly character based, and I can't imagine it any other way. Characterization was <i>not</i> a strong point of Partials. I never heavily connected to the characters, but I was SO captivated by their surroundings and their story.<br> <br>The tone of this book felt more like a science-based procedural crime show set in a post-apocalyptic world populated by cyborgs and a few remaining humans. This is Battlestar Galactica if Battlestar Galatica had been written by the writers of Bones.<br><br><b>
  <u>Characterization and Romance</u>
</b><br><br>The weak link in Partial's chain was it's characterization. It's written in third person and I found it difficult to truly hear the voices of the characters. In fact, the only one I ever emotional connected to was the one that wasn't even human: the Partial that we meet later on, Samm. <i>But</i> considering that I am actually a cylon, you could say we share a certain kinship and all.<br><br>The Senate, Kira's arch nemesis, is full of people who are delusional and one-dimensional, seeming to be so set in their ways that they don't care if it destroys them.<br><br>Romance does not play much of a part AT ALL in this novel. It's an extra, meandering about in the background, sipping it's vente chai soy latte and speaking in a fake British accent. In fact, I couldn't have been less interested in the so-called "romantic" storyline between Kira and Marcus.  But even so, this book and it's story managed to transcend it's characters.<br><br><b>
  <u>Does this put the SCI in SCI-FI?</u>
</b><br><br>This is pretty hard science fiction... for YA. Don't get me wrong, I've definitely seen harder.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362611i/713784.jpg" width="320" height="292" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Did you know that robots now play ping pong? And have ROCK HARD ABS?! Humina humina.</i><br><br><i>But</i> that's usually in adult fiction, so this is a welcome move into the realm of young adult novels. <u>Partials is an excellent choice for fans of "sciencey" science fiction.</u> (That's me!) Kira spends time actually asking questions and analyzing data. And I loved every minute of it. Amazingly and most importantly, I felt like I understood it all.<br><br>I don't really know anything about how viruses work. But when reading this book, I am operating on the assumption that the author writing about viruses knows <i>at least</i> more than I do. That being said, I felt Dan Wells did an amazing job at breaking down the science, especially toward the end. <br><br>I had a lot of questions while reading. <i>Why do the babies get sick only after they are born? If the virus is airborne, why couldn't the babies survive in a filtered clean room?</i> Conveniently enough, Kira had a lot of the same questions and managed to answer many of my concerns.<br><br>I've recently come to the realization that my obsession with literature stems from a quest for knowledge. I constantly feel the need to learn and grow and change. To see and imagine new things. I feel like this is one of those novels. One of those novels that attempts to push thinking forward, that focuses on the questions of life, as opposed to the problems in it.<br><br>Many post-apocalyptic novels are problem based, not question based. They encounter a problem and they push through. In Partials, Kira encounters a question and she <i>answers</i> it. A problem is just something that you have to work through and solve. You either solve it or you don't. A question is something that opens up a whole new realm of possibilities. Questions are often accompanied by their own problems, however. <u>This is a story about solutions. Solutions to the questions asked and to the problems that come along with it.</u><br><br><i>The mark of a great science fiction author is having the ability to make the reader believe that they are a freaking <b>rocket scientist</b>.</i> Or in the case of this book... A virologist. Write it <i>so</i> well that the reader is sciencing that science right along with the main characters. Dan Wells certainly excelled at doing just that.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Pacing</u>
</b><br><br>I started this book with a straight face. Twenty five percent in, I was pursing my lips in question. Fifty percent in, I was nodding my head in agreement. Seventy five percent in, I was grinning with excitement. At the end, I was passed out from exhaustion and amazement.<br><br>The story moves along consistently, but not at a breakneck pace either. It has quite a bit of action and a constant crawl of information.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Verdict</u>
</b><br><br>Partials is a dense post-apocalyptic delicious dessert, swirled with dystopian undertones, and topped off with dark military themes. Who wouldn't want a piece of that?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362611i/713785.jpg" width="224" height="209" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Well, what do you know? There's actually a <a href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0762441062/ref=as_li_ss_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;tag=findthebook-20&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;camp=1789&amp;creative=390957&amp;creativeASIN=0762441062" rel="nofollow noopener">BOOK</a><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362611i/713786.gif" width="1" height="1" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> for that!</i><br><br>I worry that it may have a hard time finding an audience as a young adult book because it is so heavily grounded in science. Sci-fi in YA excites me, and this book was a great start to what is hopefully a new trend in the young adult world.<br><br>The story is not character or romance based, but it is high in <u>concept, plot and science</u>. It is also not a standalone as I previously assumed, seeing as it ends on a semi-cliffhanger. It is questioning, yet not too philosophical. Light cerebral sci-fi.<br><br>If you're looking at experimenting with science fiction (And, come on, science fiction and experimentation go GREAT together!), <b>Partials would be an excellent place to start.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13647369130425585867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_270541347" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270541347" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270541347?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=free-from-work">free-from-work</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=the-end">the-end</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer270541347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6231898566592715871">oh my god!! i just got an unexpected ARC of this on the SAME DAY as i got the new ron rash ARC!!! what is a girl to do??? too many good things at once!!! this is the best nightmare i have ever had!<br/><br/>____________________________________________________________<br/><br/>this is a very high three-stars. it would have been a four if i was just judging it on enjoyment and the ability of the plot to engage me. but i have decided to be more responsible when reviewing the YA, and not just letting it get away with s</span>
  <span id="freeText6231898566592715871" style="display:none">oh my god!! i just got an unexpected ARC of this on the SAME DAY as i got the new ron rash ARC!!! what is a girl to do??? too many good things at once!!! this is the best nightmare i have ever had!<br><br>____________________________________________________________<br><br>this is a very high three-stars. it would have been a four if i was just judging it on enjoyment and the ability of the plot to engage me. but i have decided to be more responsible when reviewing the YA, and not just letting it get away with stuff just because its intended audience is probably going to let it get away with stuff. since the lines between YA and adult fiction keep getting more and more blurred, and since dan wells has written primarily for adults before this, my hammer is coming down.<br><br>exposition is tough. catching a reader up to the action occurring in the novel's "past," particularly in dystopian settings where it is bound to be complicated, is tricky. but this isn't a movie. a book has the advantage of not having to do this in dialogue. and when you do choose to do it in dialogue, it just sounds clunky.<br><br><b>character one:</b> remember five years ago when this thing happened??<br><br><b>character two:</b> i do, but then that other thing happened so it made it somehow worse, but we were able to do blank which prevented us from blankety-blanking.<br><br><b>character one:</b> right, but we forgot about that other thing.<br><br><b>character two:</b> yeah, that was rough.<br><br>i mean - that is just an example of how awkward this kind of thing can be - it is obviously not as bad in the book, but it rankles nonetheless to have characters sitting around discussing events they lived through as though giving a memorized oral report on historical events.it just works better to have characters thinking these things to themselves. benefit of the medium - ca$h in on it. <br><br>the other complaint i have, and this might be unavoidable in YA lit of this kind, is how much agency these kids have. i understand that in a world like this, there would be necessary adaptation, and a heightening of responsibility and maturity, but little teens in business suits and briefcases working in the senate? rising to power in the military? curing cancer? it just seems too fantastic. and our sixteen-year-old heroine is the one to point out the very obvious blind spot in the scientists' research thus far? they spent eleven years performing the exact same tests without ever thinking of that? it just seems unlikely that the scientists are that terrible at their jobs.<br><br>and what are the rest of the survivors doing? there are three foci: government.military. doctors/scientists.where is everyone else? who is picking up the trash? did i miss where all the food is coming from? besides the herbs? although i am actually pretty glad that he explained the clothing thing, because it is simple and a cool detail that is never really touched upon in most the the stuff i have been reading. this kind of detail is not important to a lot of people, but i really like aftermath stories, particularly when the details of its restructuring are included. they are not necessary to tell this story, but i do appreciate it when a world built is built densely.<br><br>okay - enough nitpicking. because there is plenty of good stuff here. for all the lack in the world-building, there is plenty of detail in the virology elements. a lot of books like this would skimp on the details, and just say, "it is a viiiirus. it makes our babies diieeeee." and not go into why. this does. it is cleverly done, and makes sense, as far as my science-free brain is concerned. this is what made the mira grant books so strong - explanation of how things came to be in a respectable white lab coat. i am on board.<br><br>action sequences - also good. everything that happened on manhattan was well-written and gripping - i appreciated all the twists and turns and ambiguity. and then that thing that happens to her in the lab with the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[zzzzzzzzt! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - fantastically jarring, that.<br><br>characters are mostly good: haru specifically is well-done - there is a lot of shadow in that character, and i really appreciated the murkiness and inscrutability. kira as true-believer is an archetype that can get old pretty fast, but at least she is action, and not just all talk. <br><br>aside: i'm not crazy about racial checklist books: one of <i>these</i> and one of <i>those</i> and don't forget to include a <i>this</i> and <i>that</i> mix. it just strikes me as disingenuous and pandering. <br><br>he is completely right about the names of towns of long island. ronkonkoma? ridiculous. <br><br>and am i the only one for whom <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the destruction of all that medical equipment is a really big deal? that isn't going to be replaced. there is no one left to make those things anymore. what is going to happen with that? this is a tiny detail that is causing me conniptions. what will happen?? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>twists: also done well. especially the one you know which one i am talking about. when that part happened, i literally sat straight up and said, "iiiinteresting" and my brain started racing towards all the places this could go and getting excited to see how the rest of the series will play out. <br><br>so - yeah. ultimately, a high-three from me. but with such spectacular potential for future books. i really think this is just a matter of an author trying to fit themselves into the expectations of YA and having a reasonable amount of turbulence. on the one hand - this is definitely not dumbed-down for its audience. on the other, there are just some structural oversights and missteps. but a really fun book with a great future ahead of itself.<br><br>maybe not a great future for the characters muahahahahahaa<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6231898566592715871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_224918188" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224918188" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/224918188?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer224918188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13471318317635219038">Intense with highly sophisticated world building- Partials is a fantastic addition to the dystopian genre. Babies don't survive and the youngest human on earth is now 14 years old. With 99% of the population gone, killed by a new epidemic, Kira is determined to find a cure to save humanity.<br/><br/>I have to start with Kira because she is an excellent protagonist. She is incredibly determined, and this presence throughout the novel of pure dedication to her cause is all consuming. You want her to succeed</span>
  <span id="freeText13471318317635219038" style="display:none">Intense with highly sophisticated world building- Partials is a fantastic addition to the dystopian genre. Babies don't survive and the youngest human on earth is now 14 years old. With 99% of the population gone, killed by a new epidemic, Kira is determined to find a cure to save humanity.<br /><br />I have to start with Kira because she is an excellent protagonist. She is incredibly determined, and this presence throughout the novel of pure dedication to her cause is all consuming. You want her to succeed so badly that it becomes a truly captivating read. This is not her only quality; she is also strong, confident and outspoken. These are all traits that make a well-rounded, easy to root for protagonist if you ask me. I clicked with her almost instantly. She is shadowed by quite a few secondary characters as well who are equally of value to the story. Some of them are more developed than others, but they all have great personalities that really fill up the pages.<br /><br />One thing that stands out from this book that actually surprised me, is the lack of a romantic plot. Yes the protagonist has a boyfriend, but we barely see them together. She's not one to forget that this is the end of the world because a cute boy happens to pass by. The plot - saving humanity - comes first! Surprising right? I do enjoy romance, but I was relieved to see that, finally, we've got a dystopian not powered by a love story. <br /><br />I had heard this novel was a bit on the scientific side which made me a bit wary because me and science are not great friends. Therefore, I surprise even myself when I say that the science added to the story is what makes it the most interesting. It turns everything that is happening in this future world completely realistic, and truly alarming. Instead of simply being told that there is a virus without a cure, killing all our babies, we go in deeper with Kira researching what exactly is happening inside our bodies, and why a cure still hasn't been found in over a decade. It's not overwhelming by any means. It was neither confusing, nor boring. The only thing it made me, was fascinated.<br /><br />The Partials almost made us extinct, the Voice is rebelling against the few surviving humans, this leaves us with a story full of villains. What does this promise? Intensity! It does take a little bit to get into a fast pace, but once it does it's especially action packed until the very end. We also quickly realize that there is no clear picture on who the enemy really is, or who we should trust. This essentially turns an already exciting plot into an intense roller coaster ride full of fear, uncertainty and surprise. With no shortage of dystopian novels on the shelves nowadays, make sure that this one ends up on yours! <br /><br />--<br />For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Xpresso Reads</b>
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13471318317635219038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer8572313189576511908">A few annoyances (like the oft-mentioned kudzu. WE GET IT.) but I found this really enjoyable!     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_413466817" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/413466817" />
    <a title="Nickie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10632371-nickie"><img alt="Nickie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442646242p2/10632371.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/413466817?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nickie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nickie" href="/user/show/10632371-nickie">Nickie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer413466817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15323742504033441410">I feel like this review should begin like one of the old AlkaSeltzer commercials.<br/><br/>"I can't believe I read the whole thing."<br/><br/>I try to be balanced on my reviews, but this book made it very difficult. There were a million little things that got under my skin, and it added up to a book that didn't make sense and was ultimately unlikable.<br/><br/>What I liked about this book:<br/>The genre? I guess? Although, reading this had made me rethink that decision.<br/> <br/>What I didn't like about this book:<br/>Hoo boy, where do I start</span>
  <span id="freeText15323742504033441410" style="display:none">I feel like this review should begin like one of the old AlkaSeltzer commercials.<br /><br />"I can't believe I read the whole thing."<br /><br />I try to be balanced on my reviews, but this book made it very difficult. There were a million little things that got under my skin, and it added up to a book that didn't make sense and was ultimately unlikable.<br /><br />What I liked about this book:<br />The genre? I guess? Although, reading this had made me rethink that decision.<br /> <br />What I didn't like about this book:<br />Hoo boy, where do I start? The little things really killed this book for me. Writing fiction is all about suspending disbelief. If you're going to throw me into an entirely fictional world of your vision, you have to paint a compelling pictures, keep your world building consistent, and make your characters fit into that world for me to buy it.<br /><br />Every few pages I ran into some little thing that just pulled me out of the story. The suspension of disbelief never last more than 5 pages, and then I was back at square one. Allow me to list some examples.<br /><br />1. (My biggest beef with this book) Imagine *Society* has collapsed. 99.9% of all humankind has died from a virus. You probably won't be getting electricity, and you're definitely going to have to fend for yourself. Everybody died quickly, in their homes and in their place of business, from a terrible plague. Where, oh where in the great nation of the United States of America, would you think to settle yourself?<br /><br />Somewhere with a low population so you don't have to bury too many dead? Somewhere with nice weather, you say? With fertile lands and plentiful hunting grounds? With access to clean water? Why, how sensible of you. Too bad all the remaining humans decided to move to New York City without you. You die!<br /><br />******Seriously, this bugged me the ENTIRE time I was reading this book. Why would they move to New York City? Why? How does that even make sense? It's never explained********<br /><br />2. The second major conflict in the book is that humans have not been able to successfully reproduce since the onset of the plague. Babies are carried to term, but become infected with the virus almost immediately after birth and die within days.<br /><br />In response, the government has mandated that all women 18 and older do their part to conceive as many children as possible (you know, take a run at statistics). How many children is enough for the government, you ask?<br /><br />Why, little lady, you only have to get pregnant once a year for the rest of your fertile days! That's totally reasonable, right?<br /><br />This is where it became painfully obvious to me that this story was written by a man. There's just so much wrong with this. Pregnancy is more than just squeezing out a baby. It has to develop for nine months, which literally depletes nutrients from a woman's body. Women who have too frequent pregnancies or pregnancies too close to each other run into a whole host of potential health problems (OB/GYNs generally recommend 18 months between pregnancies, not 3!!! What the heck.)<br /><br />So this society is on the brink of collapse, and they're willing to risk the health of the entire female population. Yep. Gotcha.<br /><br />3. The slang in the book killed me. The book begins 15 years after the plague, so there's no TV, no magazines, no internet. Yet Kira described one of her friends as having a 'supermodel flat' stomach. Seriously? Why would Kira be familiar with supermodels?<br /><br />Etc. etc. etc.<br /><br /><br />**************<br /><br />This review will be a mile long if I list every little thing that annoyed me, so I'll stop there. The point is, every time I read something totally off kilter, I paused, put the book down for a moment, and said 'What?' I kept getting pulled out of the story, which is the exact opposite of the desired effect. The story needs to pull me in. I found that the little things made it impossible for me to ever get settled in Kira's world.<br /><br />Final verdict: <br />Save yourself some heartache and skip this book. If you really need to read about plague survivors, pick up Stephen King's 'The Stand' instead. If you want to read about almost-human clones, grab a copy of 'Do Androids Dream of Electric Sheep?' Those are classics for a reason, and 'Partials' doesn't come anywhere near these two. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15323742504033441410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_239569339" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239569339" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/239569339?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=arc-galley-or-author">arc-galley-or-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=male-approved">male-approved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239569339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9975795157030230933">Oh, wait while I find my mouth under my bed where it dropped.<br/><br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/dan-wells/review-partials.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363781i/715279.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>..So, are you ready for this wonderful journey into the future?<br/>Here we go…<br/><br/>It all came down to a war - the worst of them all.<br/>It was not between humans, but between them and the Partials.<br/>Because what if robots didn’t look like robots anymore?<br/>What if they looked exactly like humans? What if they were genetically programmed and made into the best weapon alive, a dangerously thinking one? Breathing flesh-and-blood robots meant to kill -</span>
  <span id="freeText9975795157030230933" style="display:none">Oh, wait while I find my mouth under my bed where it dropped.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/dan-wells/review-partials.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363781i/715279.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>..So, are you ready for this wonderful journey into the future?<br>Here we go…<br><br>It all came down to a war - the worst of them all.<br>It was not between humans, but between them and the Partials.<br>Because what if robots didn’t look like robots anymore?<br>What if they looked exactly like humans? What if they were genetically programmed and made into the best weapon alive, a dangerously thinking one? Breathing flesh-and-blood robots meant to kill - stronger and faster than us.<br>What if they’ve decided to take over the world?<br>What if they’ve almost succeeded?<br>What if humanity would be collapsing each day?<br>Well... Here's where the story begins...<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I lost my father, my mother, my wife, my children, my friends, neighbors, patients, colleagues, students. I was in a hospital at the time; I watched it fill up and spill over until there weren't even enough survivors to carry away the corpses. I watched my entire world eat itself alive, Walker, while you were playing with your dolls. So don't tell me I'm not doing enough to save the human race, and don't you dare tell me we can risk another Partial War."</i>
</blockquote><br>It’s not only that the premise was absolutely wonderful; it’s the fact that the whole book is so amazing.<br>I am not going to tell you too much about the story, because you need to read it by yourself, I am just going to keep telling you about all the things I liked about it.<br><br>Yes, I must confess that it was a bit slow for my taste in the first half, but by the ending I needed to remind myself to breath – because the action was breathtaking, with so many turnarounds, so many new informations about the this world, and the insecurity was killing me (not knowing who’s bad, who’s god, who’s gonna betray next).<br>There were so many questions I had not only about the Partials but also about the humans. I got some of the answers, but also the number of questions started to grow with every page, keeping me on the edge of my seat.<br>There were many people comparing this series with <a title="Newsflesh" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/tag/newsflesh" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Newsflesh</a> by Mira Grant, and they are quite right. I thought about it too while reading this book. There is this big challenge to find a cure, and to discover all the dirty politics and the people behind them all. It also has the same feeling and many of you might like it just as much. I know I did.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"It had been easier, in some ways, when Kira was a kid and the Partials were the big bad guy. Everything terrible that had happened could be explained, and while the explanation might be scary, at least it was simple. Darkness was clearly divided from light. These days... Kira had no idea who the enemy was, or who you could blame, or who you could trust."</i>
</blockquote><br>There were not many characters that I got to really care about, but for the first time it didn’t bother me (there were many other things to keep me entertained).<br><br>From the beginning we are introduced to Kira and her friends and family. I really liked her for being smart, strong, and mature for her age. Even though some times her actions brought her more trouble then needed, she always had the very best intentions. She cared about her people and the future of humanity.<br>Her story with her boyfriend didn’t hold my attention, but it helped us see another side of her. Also, all her discoveries were surprising even for me, and now I am more interested then never to know her better.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Forget love, forget freedom, forget choice, just get yourself knocked up and save the damn world already"</i>
</blockquote><br>Talking about intriguing characters, I should mention of course Samm - a Partial about to turn Kira’s world upside down. Every time I thought I’ve figured him out something happened, changing my mind completely (not always in a good way, but still).<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Was that your plan?" asked Kira bitterly. "To use us as slaves? As labor to maintain your infrastructure?"<br>"You mean the same thing you have done to us?"</i>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://vahlre.deviantart.com/art/The-Patient-and-His-Doctor-256997960" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363781i/715280._SX540_.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>There are some pieces missing from this puzzle, but this was a great first book in the series, and I can't wait to find out what happens next. I am all on the Partials’ side, but still I want our people to survive, so I’m a bit conflicted.<br><br>Anyways, if you want a story full of adrenaline and plot twists, this one is for you. A great dystopian, post-apocalyptic world that promises a lot in the next installments :)<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/dan-wells/review-partials.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i><br><br><i>Book source: ARC from the publisher via Netgalley. Thank you!</i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>

<div id="review_839054963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/839054963" />
    <a title="Kassidy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8937622-kassidy"><img alt="Kassidy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585073850p2/8937622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/839054963?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kassidy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kassidy" href="/user/show/8937622-kassidy">Kassidy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8937622-kassidy?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer839054963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8950056441335063331">This book is so much fun!!<br/>The plot is crazy and there is so much action. <br/>I am a Biochemistry major and I love science, and this book had a ton of science in it. There is a virus called RM that inhibits babies from living past a couple of hours, so a large portion of the book is dedicated to finding a cure for this. It goes pretty in depth with the research and specifics of the virus and I just think that's so cool :) <br/><br/>I did like the main character Kira, although she was annoying at points because</span>
  <span id="freeText8950056441335063331" style="display:none">This book is so much fun!!<br />The plot is crazy and there is so much action. <br />I am a Biochemistry major and I love science, and this book had a ton of science in it. There is a virus called RM that inhibits babies from living past a couple of hours, so a large portion of the book is dedicated to finding a cure for this. It goes pretty in depth with the research and specifics of the virus and I just think that's so cool :) <br /><br />I did like the main character Kira, although she was annoying at points because she had to save EVERYONE, even if it was a lost cause. Sometimes I just wanted to knock her in the head. She is really smart though and I enjoyed her personality. This book isn't as much character driven as plot driven, so I don't see myself getting real attached to the characters, which is kind of a downside.<br /><br />I just loved the plot developments and twists, there were points where I was just like "oh my gosh", it was awesome. There are so many mysteries and secrets in this apocalyptic world, it was so exciting figuring them all out! It literally keeps you guessing the whole time!!! I have no idea who the real enemy is.<br /><br />If you like science, science fiction, or apocalyptic stories, I would highly recommend this book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8950056441335063331" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_283223032" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/283223032" />
    <a title="Nafiza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2483439-nafiza"><img alt="Nafiza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529831446p2/2483439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/283223032?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nafiza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nafiza" href="/user/show/2483439-nafiza">Nafiza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2483439-nafiza?shelf=source-net-galley">source-net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2483439-nafiza?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer283223032" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16078813555842925143">The YA genre is certainly rife with dystopians. You can't go out without tripping over one. Okay fine, that is an exaggeration but I can't help but get weary of the same plots with a few subtle differences (you know, differences like the cause of the ultimate breakdown of modern society). There's usually a girl. She usually has powers. There's also usually a society with tyrannical rulers/dictators/whatever you wanna call them (a rose by any other name and all...). Then there is a boy. Mysteriou</span>
  <span id="freeText16078813555842925143" style="display:none">The YA genre is certainly rife with dystopians. You can't go out without tripping over one. Okay fine, that is an exaggeration but I can't help but get weary of the same plots with a few subtle differences (you know, differences like the cause of the ultimate breakdown of modern society). There's usually a girl. She usually has powers. There's also usually a society with tyrannical rulers/dictators/whatever you wanna call them (a rose by any other name and all...). Then there is a boy. Mysterious. Intriguing. Attractive. Whom the girl will feel attracted to against her will. And who will make her see her the things wrong with the system she has been blissfully living in. Okay fine, not blissfully. Let's say complacently. How does that sound? Good? Okay. <br /><br />There, I have described the majority of dystopians out there. It's almost formulaic. I'm almost ready for it to be a girl the other girl is attracted to. Or a robot. A cyborg! (Though, I'd say Prince Kai already has that down, hur.)<br /><br />Anyway, to the review proper now. All the things I mentioned above? The stereotypical elements of a dystopian novel? These are all present in <i>Partials</i>. But you know what? They all work splendidly together to create a novel that is, a lot of times, breath taking. And no, I'm not even being cheesy (okay maybe I am, slightly) saying that but it's just. Well. <br /><br /><i>Partials</i>, as all really good dystopians do, gives a peek at a future that may very well be our own. It really could be taken as a warning to all the scientists out there, you know, the ones playing God. Please be careful with whatever you are genetically creating. Seriously. <br /><br />Anyway, <i>Partials</i> is really, really entertaining. Since I said two reallys, you know I mean serious business. There is wit, there is a touch of romance with Marcus and a whole promise of more romance with Samm. There is intrigue and boy, is there action. Lots of action. Casualties. Too many and some of them were senseless. So on a purely shallow level, I was very satisfied by <i>Partials</i>. It promised to be entertaining and it was. Very. The writing was sharp (and I mean this as an adjective to describe how very readable the novel was), the plot was well constructed and the pacing was spot on. Totally awesomesauce.<br /><br />But. Well, you knew it was coming. I had some troubles with the novel. Not huge troubles. Just ones that niggle at me until I speak them out. And this may be because I analyze novels on a daily basis and I can't let a passage pass me by without analyzing the hell out of it but...I felt that the synopsis or rather the excerpt that we read on the back cover of the novel, you know, the final words of the last president? The gravitas conveyed by his final message, the sorrow, the melancholy, the loss, the utter devastation...these elements were subsumed by the overly action oriented novel. I liked the action, I did but I would have liked for us to take a breath and dwell on the immense loss of humanity. And perhaps it's just me, but I felt distanced from all the characters in the novel. As though there was something that kept me from getting inside their heads and knowing what they were thinking and feeling and I didn't like that. It kept me from connecting to them which in turn kept me from empathizing with them and all these things interfered with my final enjoyment of the novel. <br /><br />Sometimes you read a book and it resonates within you; you keep on thinking about it. I remember being affected by Birthmarked by Caragh O'Brian (we will forget book the two exists) but I didn't quite get the same feeling from <i>Partials</i>. Maybe it was because I went in expecting quite a different novel than I got. <br /><br />That being said, I still enjoyed the novel tremendously. In fact, I think this will make a kick ass movie. Is someone out there listening? You could sell millions. Anyway, I am definitely reading the second one in the series and I wholeheartedly (with ALL my heart, not just three quarters of it) recommend it to you. Yes you, the one who's still wondering. Go read this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16078813555842925143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_235142804" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/235142804" />
    <a title="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3039709-michelle-the-bookshelf-stalker-queen-of-the-undead"><img alt="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328667000p2/3039709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235142804?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead" href="/user/show/3039709-michelle-the-bookshelf-stalker-queen-of-the-undead">Michelle, the Bookshelf Stalker  Queen of the Undead</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer235142804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6391759108845524679"><i>Before you read my review…</i><br/><br/><i>I originally rated this book 4 out of 5 stars but after I wrote my review, I lowered it to 2.5 out of 5 stars (rounded up to 3 stars). My reasons… I rated the book immediately after reading it and I was clearly caught up in the last 25% of the book. When I wrote my review, I realized that the majority of my review was negative and I had plenty of issues with the story. Thus, I changed my rating.</i><br/><br/><b>
  <u>The Bad</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>I didn’t feel a real connection with the characters.</b> The real sto</span>
  <span id="freeText6391759108845524679" style="display:none"><i>Before you read my review…</i><br /><br /><i>I originally rated this book 4 out of 5 stars but after I wrote my review, I lowered it to 2.5 out of 5 stars (rounded up to 3 stars). My reasons… I rated the book immediately after reading it and I was clearly caught up in the last 25% of the book. When I wrote my review, I realized that the majority of my review was negative and I had plenty of issues with the story. Thus, I changed my rating.</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Bad</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>I didn’t feel a real connection with the characters.</b> The real story seemed centered on dying babies, half robot soldiers, isolated humans being controlled by a secretive government, and a protesting secretive group that doesn’t like the government’s control. The characters felt like they were placed in the story after the fact and could be interchanged. While, in the end, I found myself liking Kira, I didn’t feel a real connection to her. If she had died along the way, I wouldn’t have felt any real sadness. If she had turned out to be a traitor, I wouldn’t have felt any real anger. If one of the minor characters suddenly took over the story, I wouldn’t have minded.<br /><br /><b>The world building.</b> Dan Wells did his homework. He created a virus, explained it quite well, explained its impact on the world population, and came up with a creative solution to the virus. He also created a war, a fractured government, half humans, explanations for the survivors, and stories for the dead. The problem is the more he explained, the bigger the hole he created as well. While his explanations were plausible, they didn’t seem probable. I couldn’t prove him wrong (well, actually in a few areas I probably could have but I didn’t want to put forth that much work) but I was thinking in my head “ahhh, yeah, I don’t think so”. The believability factor started decreasing, the more Wells tried to explain what was going on. I almost wished he hadn’t done so much work to explain everything. Leave some to the imagination of the reader. The reader can’t argue with a writer if the explanation is in our own head.<br /><br /><b>The Good</b><br /><br /><b>The Partials.</b> I loved the entire Partials vs. Humans concept. I feel like it has been played out especially in old sci-fi shows but I still liked it. I especially loved the twist. I was even more surprised that I didn’t guess the twist. It was interesting because I pride myself on figuring twists out and this one blindsided me.<br /><br /><b>The world building.</b> I know, it is in the “Good” and in the “Bad” but you are gonna have to deal with my weird reviews. While the world building had lots of issues for me, it also was pretty impressive. Maybe I’m giving Wells kudos for effort but this IS my review so whatever.<br /><br /><b>The last 25%</b> This is really where the story began. I know that doesn’t seem like a good thing but once the action in the story took off, I found myself hooked. I stopped worrying about the credibility of the science or my ambivalence to the characters and just sat back and enjoyed the ride.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6391759108845524679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_267117331" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/267117331" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/267117331?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4016030-isamlq?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4016030-isamlq?shelf=aaw-yeah">aaw-yeah</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267117331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer290776639614668545"><b>Holy...<i>Awesome!</i> </b> <br/><br/>It’s been a <b>loooong</b> while since I’ve felt this excited about a post apoc/ dystopia YA. I thought I’d burned out on them after reading Starters and Eve and heck even Shatter Me; the lack of detail in the first two and the over indulgent writing in the other simply put me off. So I really am not kidding when I say it’s been a long time since I’ve felt this excited about a book of this type. <br/><br/>It's a little like Grant’s Feed (or Deadline) because this too does not limit itself to hea</span>
  <span id="freeText290776639614668545" style="display:none"><b>Holy...<i>Awesome!</i> </b> <br /><br />It’s been a <b>loooong</b> while since I’ve felt this excited about a post apoc/ dystopia YA. I thought I’d burned out on them after reading Starters and Eve and heck even Shatter Me; the lack of detail in the first two and the over indulgent writing in the other simply put me off. So I really am not kidding when I say it’s been a long time since I’ve felt this excited about a book of this type. <br /><br />It's a little like Grant’s Feed (or Deadline) because this too does not limit itself to heart pumping chase scenes and big explosions (though there was plenty of the same here.) And if Feed had George and Shaun mixed in a plot of more than just one thing, PARTIALS was a little like that by going into the usual elements but delving deeper into each without sacrificing the pace. Specifically, it tackled the virus bit that most post apocs have beyond the superficial level; there was lot of detail (that likely went over my head); yet I did appreciate the lengths to which most things were explained. <br /><br />There are sides in this one too. It’s is so much more than a story of the fight/plight of a rebelling faction; or even just that of controlling higher ups. There’s more than two sides here. And I liked how each side made the story more than just a little complicated. One thing is for sure, I was focused on trying to figure what the real deal was and who the real baddie was, or at least who the greater evil was. I mean it’s obvious that the Senate was up to no good, but like I said some of them could be passionate and fiery about their stand and sometimes effectively convincing. Then with the slow unfolding of one plan then another plan then yet another? OK, just color me impressed. <br /><br />It’s split in several parts and in each part I found something that I enjoyed. Part one introduces some very passionate people who, I’ll be honest had me raising some questions. Mainly that they’re all so young and yet all sounded so old! BUT after considering the context, the when/where /how of the way they were living in, they actually did make sense. Given that, I was very impressed by the passion they showed… even when they disagreed, no, especially when they disagreed. With each argument, I got pulled in then understood where each was coming from, then ended up not quite sure about who to side with. My favorite moments though were towards the end. Those twists? I knew they were coming, but still… Awesome, anyone? <br /><br />And it could get scary at times. There are more than a couple of things in this one that were scary. Why is it that in books like these, it’s the women who have to bear the brunt? The scary bits aren’t even about the virus or the humanoid soldiers (fascinating though those may be); the terrifying bit was when it touched on weighing a person’s liberties versus the “good” of all, reminding me a little of Offred and her story. <br /><br />Want.next.one.now.<br /><br /><b>3.5-4/5<br />Thanks Netgalley!</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="290776639614668545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
