<div id="review_287772986" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/287772986" />
    <a title="Jacquelyn Sylvan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1015008-jacquelyn-sylvan"><img alt="Jacquelyn Sylvan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375401621p2/1015008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/287772986?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacquelyn Sylvan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacquelyn Sylvan" href="/user/show/1015008-jacquelyn-sylvan">Jacquelyn Sylvan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1015008-jacquelyn-sylvan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1015008-jacquelyn-sylvan?shelf=my-favorite-books-of-2012">my-favorite-books-of-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1015008-jacquelyn-sylvan?shelf=books-read-in-2013">books-read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer287772986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9241289851505868384">How do I love thee, Partials? Let me count the ways….<br/><br/>1)<b>Thy witty, spicy dialogue.</b> If you’re a fan of Firefly/Serenity or Buffy the Vampire Slayer’s (the show, not the movie) whip-sharp banter, you’re going to love this book. It’s got the same kind of effortless, rapid-fire discourse Joss Whedon injects in his cult-classic shows. A lot of authors shoot for this and fail miserably; Wells doesn’t just succeed, he excels at dialogue. I could seriously have read and enjoyed this book purely for the b</span>
  <span id="freeText9241289851505868384" style="display:none">How do I love thee, Partials? Let me count the ways….<br /><br />1)<b>Thy witty, spicy dialogue.</b> If you’re a fan of Firefly/Serenity or Buffy the Vampire Slayer’s (the show, not the movie) whip-sharp banter, you’re going to love this book. It’s got the same kind of effortless, rapid-fire discourse Joss Whedon injects in his cult-classic shows. A lot of authors shoot for this and fail miserably; Wells doesn’t just succeed, he excels at dialogue. I could seriously have read and enjoyed this book purely for the banter. <br /><br />2)<b>Thy heroine be neither ninny nor copycat.</b> I never thought I’d say this, but…Katniss, this girl Kira could kick your ass. Kira’s genius-level smart, loyal, brave, stubborn—and, though we’ve seen these characteristics a million, billion times, somehow wholly unique. Maybe because Kira’s not running around trying to sacrifice herself for a boy; she chooses the cause every time, no matter what the cost. And, on that note:<br /><br />3)<b>Thou art a great crossover book for boys.</b> I don’t care what authors and publishers say; there’s too much romance in mainstream YA to make it attractive to boys of the same age group. The romance in Partials, though, is minimal. Kira is already involved in a healthy relationship when we meet her, and the introduction of Samm doesn’t threaten that relationship—at least, not in the way we’re used to seeing. Don’t get me wrong, I enjoy sampling the fruits of forbidden and/or starcrossed love as much as the next YA reader—but I didn’t realize how burned out on breaths catching and long, meaningful stares I was until they weren’t there, and I felt refreshed by their lack. So, if you’re looking for a book for a teenage boy, one that has hardly any mushy scenes, but many gunfights and military maneuvers and escapes by sea and ASPLOSIONS—get him Partials. <br /><br />4)<b>Thou makest science fiction easy and fun.</b> I was a little nervous when I realized how important virology was going to be to the plot. I like a little science in my books—it adds to the realism—but lots of books go overboard on the intricacies of the science, and then I just get confused. But Partials took a complex idea and broke it down into smaller, digestible pieces. I understood it without feeling talked down to, and therefore my enjoyment of the story and all its implications wasn’t dulled. <br /><br />5)<b>Thou layest thy foreshadowing with a light hand on the brush.</b> It’s annoying to predict how the book is going to end within the first three chapters and then, three hundred pages later, find out you were completely right. Partials has two major plot twists. One I sort of saw coming, but the clues were so subtle, and buried in conflicting information, that I doubted myself until the reveal. The other I was completely blindsided by—but when I found it, I was annoyed that I hadn’t guessed it earlier, because everything I needed to figure it out was there all along. <br /><br />And there you have it—a book that I’m going to go out on a limb and include in my top five of 2012, even though we’re not even a quarter of the way through yet. Please to enjoy.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9241289851505868384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_269933584" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/269933584" />
    <a title="Debbie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5098369-debbie"><img alt="Debbie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589209937p2/5098369.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/269933584?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie " href="/user/show/5098369-debbie">Debbie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269933584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17058998759008439550">I’m sitting here, trying to figure out how to write a review for this amazing novel. The awesome author, Dan Wells, has totally blown me away. Partials is an incredibly amazing world and storyline with fantastic characters. I can't even pick which is my favorite. Dan Wells gave all of them terrific personalities: Kira is head-strong, Marcus is the fun guy, Jayden is a take charge guy, Xochi is the bad-ass chick, Madison is the caring mom figure, Haru is the jerk, Isolde is a analyst and Samm is </span>
  <span id="freeText17058998759008439550" style="display:none">I’m sitting here, trying to figure out how to write a review for this amazing novel. The awesome author, Dan Wells, has totally blown me away. Partials is an incredibly amazing world and storyline with fantastic characters. I can't even pick which is my favorite. Dan Wells gave all of them terrific personalities: Kira is head-strong, Marcus is the fun guy, Jayden is a take charge guy, Xochi is the bad-ass chick, Madison is the caring mom figure, Haru is the jerk, Isolde is a analyst and Samm is a Partial with heart. I love, LOVE this book and wish I had an inside connection with Dan Wells so I wouldn't have to wait for Failsafe, the second book in the Partials series.<br /><br />Kira is sixteen and a medic trainee in the hospital maternity ward. Kira, along with the rest of her race, who have survived the Break, are trying to find the cure for the RM virus that still continues to kill their babies. Kira is determined to find the cure, and once she starts the search, she has no idea how far she will delve into the government, the Partials, the humans, and herself to find the answers.<br /><br />Partials is also action-packed, but Wells did bring romance into this fantastic storyline, which I'm so glad he did. And what a heartfelt romance it is with Kira and Marcus. I did, at times, think Wells was going to change Kira's romantic interest, and I’m still not sure he won't in Failsafe. I'll just have to wait and see. Wells also brings heart-break with plenty of tears with one of the character (no spoilers) I will just say, I really loved this guy.<br /><br />Dan Wells’ dedication in Partials is the best way to describe my own feelings for this amazing novel: “This book is dedicated to the rule breakers, the troublemakers, and the revolutionaries. Sometimes the hand that feeds you needs a good bite.” I highly, highly recommend Partials as a must read. You don't won't to miss out on this book! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17058998759008439550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1327973885" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1327973885" />
    <a title="Darren Hagan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34101852-darren-hagan"><img alt="Darren Hagan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436632030p2/34101852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1327973885?book_show_action=true">Jul 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darren Hagan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darren Hagan" href="/user/show/34101852-darren-hagan">Darren Hagan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007465224" href="/book/show/13509092-partials">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1327973885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16466381667046248789">**4.5 stars**<br/>**No spoilers**<br/><br/>This book was a really nice surprise. I think I must not have read the synopsis clearly when I bought it because I thought it was a book where aliens had taken over the world and there were only one community of humans left. But yeah, not at all. In a way I think that helped me to like it so much, because I was surprised whilst reading it. Maybe I should try and do that more often...<br/><br/>Anyway, I thought the plot was really interesting as I've not read anything about gene</span>
  <span id="freeText16466381667046248789" style="display:none">**4.5 stars**<br />**No spoilers**<br /><br />This book was a really nice surprise. I think I must not have read the synopsis clearly when I bought it because I thought it was a book where aliens had taken over the world and there were only one community of humans left. But yeah, not at all. In a way I think that helped me to like it so much, because I was surprised whilst reading it. Maybe I should try and do that more often...<br /><br />Anyway, I thought the plot was really interesting as I've not read anything about genetically engineered soldiers before. Hooray for first times! The pacing was generally good, however there were a few moments when they were travelling from one place to another that just felt like it dragged on a bit too long and my attention would wander - there weren't too many of those though.<br /><br />The characters were great in my opinion. Kira is an extremely smart protagonist and her loyalty to making a better future for the human race was admirable and made me really root for her. One thing I appreciated was that she was already in a solid relationship at the start of the book, so there was no instalove to deal with. I loved her boyfriend Marcus too. They had a lot of cute and funny moments together, but he made me laugh a good few times. As did one of Kira's best friends, Xochi. <br /><br />Partials was an engrossing book and I hope the series continues to be as good. I struggle to think of how to describe it so I can recommend it. It's like an apocalyptic world (not the zombie kind, but everything has gone to crap and 99.9% of the human race have died), where everything isn't quite as it seems from the get go and there are some surprising moments. I can't really say "you'll like it if you liked this..." because I can't think what it is like. Sorry :P</span>
  <a data-text-id="16466381667046248789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Katerina  Kondrenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36306002-katerina-kondrenko"><img alt="Katerina  Kondrenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590049412p2/36306002.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1089514287?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina  Kondrenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina  Kondrenko" href="/user/show/36306002-katerina-kondrenko">Katerina  Kondrenko</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1089514287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12774928120765153281"><blockquote>
  <b>7 out of 10</b>
</blockquote><br/><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br/><a href='http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/09/crooked-kingdom-by-leigh-bardugo.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br/><br/><b>Short-Soundtrack:</b><br/><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=WpB5vcNY6uE' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hannah Georgas – Enemies (Mathbonus Remix) </a><br/><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cIWRYwCGEF4' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Royksopp ft. Robyn – The Girl And The Robot </a><br/><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fCaliFaEAgc' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lunatica – Who You Are </a><br/> <br/><b>Genre</b>: post-apocalypses dystopia, YA<br/><b>Stuff</b>: bio-humans, deadly virus<br/><b>Fail</b>: slow pacing at the start<br/><b>WOW</b>: action<br/><b>POV</b>: 3rd person, female<br/><b>Love-Geometry</b>: light<br/><br/><b>Quote-Co</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12774928120765153281" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>7 out of 10</b>
</blockquote><br /><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br /><a href="http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/09/crooked-kingdom-by-leigh-bardugo.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br /><br /><b>Short-Soundtrack:</b><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=WpB5vcNY6uE" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Hannah Georgas – Enemies (Mathbonus Remix) </a><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cIWRYwCGEF4" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Royksopp ft. Robyn – The Girl And The Robot </a><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fCaliFaEAgc" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Lunatica – Who You Are </a><br /> <br /><b>Genre</b>: post-apocalypses dystopia, YA<br /><b>Stuff</b>: bio-humans, deadly virus<br /><b>Fail</b>: slow pacing at the start<br /><b>WOW</b>: action<br /><b>POV</b>: 3rd person, female<br /><b>Love-Geometry</b>: light<br /><br /><b>Quote-Core</b>: <blockquote>
  <i>“Sometimes the hand that feeds you needs a good bite.”</i>
</blockquote><br />It was a slow start but near to 40% I got it. Also I got a taste of men’s writing style within dystopia genre and liked it. <b>Our MC is a girl but through the male’s eyes. It means no drama and a lot of action.</b><br /><br />Sometimes while reading a book you are interested in a plot but have no feelings for characters. You don’t care about their fates, relationships, lives… It’s a fail. Partials’ characters are different. With them I felt either love or hatred, there was no room for indifference. <br /><br />During this read I had no desire to pick up something else along with Partials. And now I don’t wanna put the series off, I’m gonna read it at one gulp. <br /><br /><b>The first book introduces us to a new post-apocalyptic world and to Kira.</b> She’s 16 and works in the hospital where children die almost every day because of a virus. <br /><br />All the women down to the age of 18 must give a birth to a baby as many times as possible in spite of certain death. The government, which is represented by Senate, insists on putting down this age to 16. It has no sense! <u>Why these girls should act like breeding sows when their babies die in a 2-3 days after the birth?</u> Go find the cure and then ordain a law like that. It’s stupid and pointless. Why it happens? Maybe because the real parents of these young women are dead and people who came up with such a “solution” did lost their children, thus now they don't get that pregnancy isn't a fucking shopping. 9 not very pleasant months and a very painful income. Over and over again. FUCK IT. <br /><br />Kira wants to find a cure and suggests catch up a partial to study it. Partials are dangerous, but the virus is their work (or not?) and they are immune to it. <b>Kira, her friends and her friends' friends (or not?) escape their city and go for a catching-up trip. But partials are already waiting for them…</b><br /><br />This is where I finally started to feel something toward this book. What happened after that? You should read it for yourself. As to <i>my</i>self, <b>I really enjoyed the rest of the story</b>. Sometimes I knew what was coming, in other times I had no idea what was going on. It’s a very entertaining journey. <br /><br /><b>But here is my I-don’t-understand-whys about partials.</b> At first I thought they all are men but there are women too. They’re sturdy, but feel the pain. They have feelings and after the war they wanted to go to the University. Wait a minute! Did they build up for wars? If it so then it would be more logical to create only men who don't need food (our partials do), feel no pain (so they could stand longer against their enemies), and have no hunger for knowledge (I mean this education thing). People created almost their own copies and now they are surprised that these androids rebel? I'm not.<br /><br /><i>Let’s talk about tiny details.</i><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>I love Samm.</b> He is my favorite character in this series and reminds me of the android boy from “Artificial Intelligence: AI” (I mean his nature, not the age or look) as much as of Evan Walker. C’mon, guys. You should have this feeling too! Also, Heron is very Grace-like heroine. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>I didn’t like that Kira may be a partial</b> (or is it just an imperceptible intervention in her DNA?). It’d be better if she and Samm (they should be together, you know) were on opposite sides of the barricades. Their relationships could be more complicated, intense and Romeo-&amp;-Juliette-esque. And I would love to know that Kira was kind to Samm not because of their engineering common stuff, but because of she is a good person.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<b>I hate that Jaydan died.</b> Why? Take Marcus! He’s not important for me. Jaydan was my second fav. Marcus is my never fav. It’s clear. Can we switch them, please? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And <b>I love how this book ended</b>; this kind of finals is such a great motivator to pick up the next book immediately. <br /><br /><b>Partials Sequence (Партиалы):</b><br /><blockquote>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1101333184" rel="nofollow noopener">Isolation (Изоляция)</a> #0.5/3<br />— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1089514287" rel="nofollow noopener">Partials (Партиалы)</a> #1/3<br />— Fragments (Фрагменты) #2/3<br />— Ruins (Руины) #3/3</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="12774928120765153281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_492682684" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/492682684" />
    <a title="Denisse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8759700-denisse"><img alt="Denisse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606102662p2/8759700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/492682684?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denisse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denisse" href="/user/show/8759700-denisse">Denisse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8759700-denisse?shelf=best-ya-books">best-ya-books</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer492682684" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15933668486565911982">4.5<br/><br/>OH MY JESUS CHRIST! I'M SO FANGIRLING ABOUT THIS BOOK.<br/><br/><b>Reading Partials is like James Dashner or Scott Westerfeld were teaching you immunology and virology and then taking you to this fantastic travel across a destroyed world!</b><br/><br/>This is the type of book any SCI-FI FAN would like. It has an interesting world-building, with a great backstory, amazing well developed characters, and more. <br/><br/>Also a lot of science and political stuff, not the classic <i>"horrible-abusing government"</i> but the one that could e</span>
  <span id="freeText15933668486565911982" style="display:none">4.5<br /><br />OH MY JESUS CHRIST! I'M SO FANGIRLING ABOUT THIS BOOK.<br /><br /><b>Reading Partials is like James Dashner or Scott Westerfeld were teaching you immunology and virology and then taking you to this fantastic travel across a destroyed world!</b><br /><br />This is the type of book any SCI-FI FAN would like. It has an interesting world-building, with a great backstory, amazing well developed characters, and more. <br /><br />Also a lot of science and political stuff, not the classic <i>"horrible-abusing government"</i> but the one that could emerge after a catastrophic apocalypse.<br /><br /><br /><br />El libro esta dividido en tres secciones:<br /><br />EN LA PRIMERA PARTE, tenemos a esta chica, Kira, que es una estudiante de medicina harta de ver morir a los bebes por el virus RM, del cual todos los pocos miles de humanos sobrevivientes a la Guerra Parcial son inmunes, entonces empieza a ver que no hay forma de cambiar eso con la simple LEY DE ESPERANZA, que no es otra cosa que el embarazo cuando cumples los 18, y que ahora se redujo a 16 años, lo cual es la edad de Kira. Descubre que la única forma de hacer una cura es capturar un parcial y estudiarlo, pero su Gobierno (SENADO) no la deja, así que lo hace ilegalmente para salvar al bebe de una de sus mejores amigas.<br /><br />En esta primera parte tenemos un montón de datos imnunologicos, biológicos y químicos sobre el virus, que en lo personal me fascinaron <b>La lealtad de Kira es su mayor virtud, sin ser una sufrida ni una guerrera, Kira es una gran protagonista.</b><br /><br />EN LA SEGUNDA PARTE, trata mas a fondo sobre el gobierno que se formo después de la Guerra Parcial, y los rebeldes que hay afuera. Y como afecta esto a Kira y su misión de estudiar el virus.<br /><br />El personaje de Samm es increíble, empieza misterioso, y tiene sus altos y bajas. El resto de la banda también me gusto mucho, salvo tal vez Marcus, siento que aun le falta crecer. <br /><br />EN LA TERCERA PARTE, conocemos un poco mas de los Parciales, seres creados a base de genética humana pero que son como robots-biológicos, su sociedad y que es lo que pasa con los que aun quedan ahí afuera. Se aprende mucho de su naturaleza, y es muy interesante hasta el punto de pensar "son humanos, pero con mayor resistencia y aptitudes". <br /><br />En general el libro es muy realista para ser ciencia ficción, y los personajes son creíbles, y algunos hasta divertidos. Mis favoritos sin duda son KIRA, SAMM y JAYDEN. <br /><br /><b>La historia tiene muchos temas interesantes sobre arrogancia humana, la necesidad de poder, y asuntos políticos, te hace reflexionar sobre como a veces actuamos SIN HUMANIDAD y como el abuso de poder y de inteligencia puede destruirnos.</b><br /><br />Lo único malo podría ser que el libro tiene muchas descripciones, no son aburridas, pero en mi opinión son muchas sobretodo de lo que pasa durante los tiroteos o de donde se tienen que esconder cuando están en plena acción.<br /><br /><b>En esta historia no hay buenos ni malos, solo malas y buenas decisiones.<br /><br /><u>MAS QUE UNA HISTORIA JUVENIL, ES UNA LECCIÓN DE HUMANIDAD, RESPETO Y TOLERANCIA, para aquellos que ven mas haya de solo una historia juvenil divertida</u>.</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15933668486565911982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=nook">nook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer550580480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1889164900456329949">Also reviewed for <a href='http://www.addicted2heroines.com/2013/06/review-partials-partials-sequence-1-by.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Addicted2Heroines</a>.<br/><br/>So we finally managed to engineer super-soldiers...and then they decide to revolt. <br/><i>Go figure.</i> <br/>And even though they were winning the war, they decided to release a virus that wiped out the vast majority of humanity. The humans who were resistant to the RM virus live together now, but their numbers are dwindling. Babies die within a few days of being born, and time is running out to find a cure. <br/>Kira is a sixteen year old medic who believes that the cure can be </span>
  <span id="freeText1889164900456329949" style="display:none">Also reviewed for <a href="http://www.addicted2heroines.com/2013/06/review-partials-partials-sequence-1-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Addicted2Heroines</a>.<br /><br />So we finally managed to engineer super-soldiers...and then they decide to revolt. <br /><i>Go figure.</i> <br />And even though they were winning the war, they decided to release a virus that wiped out the vast majority of humanity. The humans who were resistant to the RM virus live together now, but their numbers are dwindling. Babies die within a few days of being born, and time is running out to find a cure. <br />Kira is a sixteen year old medic who believes that the cure can be found within the Partials genetic code, and she's determined to find a subject to help her prove her theory. Unfortunately, there is a civil war brewing within her small community, and the government officials are too preoccupied with keeping the peace to listen to her. There's also the small problem of her being too young for anyone to take seriously. Once her best friend becomes pregnant, though, Kira's determination to find a way to save the babies goes into overdrive. With the help of her closest friends she sets out on a dangerous journey that will change everything, especially Kira's understanding of what it means to be human. <br /><br />I'd seen some bad reviews of this one, but it looked so darn cool that I finally decided to give it a try. I'm glad I did, because it turned out to be a good read. The characters were different than I thought they would be, and I love being surprised by things like that.<br />For example, I thought I knew how the romance would pan out. You know, the old boyfriend turns bad, and the new guy is a dream? <br />Not so much. <br />Kira's childhood sweetheart, Marcus, is really funny and laid-back. And even though I didn't feel a passionate burn coming from those two, it still felt like they needed and respected each other. <br /><i>Also, I'm a sucker for a guy with a sense of humor.</i> <br />Samm is...well, he's interesting too, but I don't want to give anything away. At any rate, the plot doesn't focus on romantic stuff as much as I thought it would. I think it's because Kira is a pretty of a self-contained character who isn't consumed by thoughts of boys. <br /><i>???<br />I know, right?! What's wrong with that girl?</i><br /><br />I also thought I had the secret twist figured out within the first few chapters. A couple of chapters later, and I just knew I was wrong. Then I was right...then I was wrong again. Every time I thought I knew what was going to happen, something would pop up and poke holes in my theory.<br /><i>Good job, Mr. Wells! You had me going in circles right up till the final GOTCHA moment!</i><br /><br />I don't recommend this if you're looking for a romance driven book, but if you've been dying to read a dystopian novel about androids taking over the world, then you may want to check this out.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1889164900456329949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11589356792607994027">Oh! My! Gosh! That was Amazing!!!<br/><br/>If you like sci-fi, post-apocalyptic, dystopian, amazing characters, action packed plot, twists that have twists, a little romance in-between things blowing up and gunshots, and just all around smart writing, put this on your to-read list! NOW!<br/><br/>Wow, this is going to be hard to do spoiler free. Here goes....<br/><br/>First let me say that the beginning of the book might be a little slow for some people. It's not one of those kind where the author takes forever to set up the </span>
  <span id="freeText11589356792607994027" style="display:none">Oh! My! Gosh! That was Amazing!!!<br /><br />If you like sci-fi, post-apocalyptic, dystopian, amazing characters, action packed plot, twists that have twists, a little romance in-between things blowing up and gunshots, and just all around smart writing, put this on your to-read list! NOW!<br /><br />Wow, this is going to be hard to do spoiler free. Here goes....<br /><br />First let me say that the beginning of the book might be a little slow for some people. It's not one of those kind where the author takes forever to set up the story, it's actually just the opposite. However, it does take a while to get going, but it is totally worth it! So don't let that deter you from reading this because once this story does get going, it does not stop!<br /><br />I'm not someone who likes to dive into a review and dissect a story character by character or plot point by plot point because I usually find that by the end of one of those reviews I have pretty much gotten an almost-spoiler free version of the story, met all the characters and learned their personalities as well. (Believe me, this is one of those stories that you could talk about forever. There are so many layers in here and so many characters that I could just write and write and share all it's awesomeness with you for days!)<br /><br />But really, I'm more of the...how did this story make me feel, kind of reviewer. What was I thinking as I read it. Would I want my friends to read this and would I like to talk about it when it's done, kind of reviewer.<br /><br />So, with all that said, this book made me feel like I wish it did not have to end. There were some great twists here...some I suspected, some I was like...WHOA! This was one of those books that had me tense, holding my breath and white knuckling the book, then shedding a few tears, then back to holding my breath. So, so good!<br /><br />Dan Wells, in my opinion, did an amazing job with each and every character, whether I like them or not. He got me invested in their stories and had me cheering for the rag tag team of rebels every step of the way. <br /><br />Book 2 can't come soon enough for me. Although, I will say that Wells left me in a pretty satisfied place while I wait, too.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /> </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_240956206" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240956206" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/240956206?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA sci-fi/dystopic fans, fans of medical thrillers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rose by: </span>
      Writing Excuses
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=ya-dystopian-books-2012">ya-dystopian-books-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=az-challenge-2012">az-challenge-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=quarterly-challenge-5-2012">quarterly-challenge-5-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer240956206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13513864226783390076">"Partials" had many elements that I absolutely loved - for the genre, for the audience, for the issues it raises and the questions that it poses for the characters within the world Dan Wells creates. Granted, some of the characters had their insufferable qualities just as realistic characters probably would when faced with the odds depicted in this novel, but man, what a ride. Each and every time I picked up this book, I did not want to put it down, and I can only think of that as a good sign.<br/><br/>I </span>
  <span id="freeText13513864226783390076" style="display:none">"Partials" had many elements that I absolutely loved - for the genre, for the audience, for the issues it raises and the questions that it poses for the characters within the world Dan Wells creates. Granted, some of the characters had their insufferable qualities just as realistic characters probably would when faced with the odds depicted in this novel, but man, what a ride. Each and every time I picked up this book, I did not want to put it down, and I can only think of that as a good sign.<br /><br />I thought a while as to how I would write a review on Dan Wells' most recent series, the first book sharing the same title as the series name. I loved the John Cleaver trilogy, which had its roots in a YA supernatural thriller that didn't let me go even after I turned the last page of the final book. "Partials" marks a turn into a different set of genres for Wells, but remains grounded with strong writing and expansion on issues I think are quite vivid and masterfully executed. It's a young adult, sci-fi/dystopian novel depicting a society that faces quite many moral divisions, yet resembles a world not unlike our own. These divisions are perceived through the eyes of a young medic, Kira Walker, who learns that everything she thinks she knows about the world around her might not be as it seems. The human race teems on the brink of extinction, thanks to a widespread virus called RM that affects the human population and makes it impossible for the human race to reproduce, and 99% of the world's population has died. She seeks to find a cure for the virus by investigating a group called the "Partials" - who are said to have engineered the virus and are immune to its effects. But time is running out as more stipulations are set for the Hope Act, and tensions are running high with groups (like the Voice) who want to see the act repealed.<br /><br />For the record, I love sci-fi that actually goes into the measure of exploring the "science" aspect of the world created. I mean, it's one thing to ask the simple question of "what if" certain elements were to occur, but to actually delve into the rationale and body of knowledge behind them is something that I don't typically see in this genre for this age group. Wells does this enough to where he's expanding upon the subject in a knowledgeable way, but the descriptions don't ever feel like they're too heavy or out of place for the context of book. It's very well researched. Some of the expansion might turn off some readers who don't necessarily like delving into the science based background of the world created within "Partials", but I. Loved. It. Every single issue, every single question about the spread of viruses that Kira asked in her pursuit to find a cure to RM were ones I asked right along with her. Virology is such a cool subject, and to be able to see it even in this bird's eye view, for however brief a time, I thought was awesome. <br /><br />It does take a while for the book to move from establishing the rules of the world and the larger cast of characters, but it's worth it when you see the underlying moral and political repercussions that Kira and her friends have to face. And to say something of the characters: it's really cool to see a proactive heroine who questions the world around her and fights for what she believes in, and even the brief romantic ties that are established in the story feel realistic and not beaten overmuch in the readers mind. True, some of the characters have their distinct flaws (Kira's combative, Marcus is resistant to change, etc.) but they feel realistic enough to follow in the parts they play in the respective story. The only thing I had some trouble with in the reading of the story is that none of the adult characters seemed to be sympathetic at all, and seemed to work against the primary characters goals the majority of the time. I think in the political, steadfast idealogies established, some of this was warranted, but I think it could've had a little better balance.<br /><br />The divide between "Partials" and humans was also refreshing to watch unfold. We're introduced to them as antagonists working against humanity, but Wells does a fine job of showing that the Partials have their own agenda and grounds for sympathy. When Kira comes across/captures one that could aid in finding a cure to RM (a boy named Samm), you follow Kira as she learns from and about him - about his secret mission, about how they're operating on their own race against time, among other aspects. There's a lot of action, betrayal, politics, science, technology, psychological turns, and character interactions in this novel that feel vivid and engaging to keep you reading until the last page.<br /><br />In sum, I really enjoyed "Partials" and eagerly await the sequel.<br /><br /><br />Overall score: 4.5/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="13513864226783390076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_774641623" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/774641623" />
    <a title="Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9219433-rebecca"><img alt="Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335970365p2/9219433.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/774641623?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca" href="/user/show/9219433-rebecca">Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer774641623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer318931455737582675">GRRRRRAAAAAARGH THIS BOOK <br/><br/>Okay. Starting to take notes, just for completeness.<br/>-Viruses don't form spores. Bacteria form spores.<br/>-Nutmeg isn't an herb, and it wouldn't be growing in an herb garden in Long Island.<br/>-"It's just like a virus, but without the virus." What the blue hell does that even mean?<br/>-A mountain lion could not kill an adult male white rhino. <br/>-There are two forms of the virus. One is airborne, one is in the blood. But somehow nobody can figure out how they're related after 11 years </span>
  <span id="freeText318931455737582675" style="display:none">GRRRRRAAAAAARGH THIS BOOK <br /><br />Okay. Starting to take notes, just for completeness.<br />-Viruses don't form spores. Bacteria form spores.<br />-Nutmeg isn't an herb, and it wouldn't be growing in an herb garden in Long Island.<br />-"It's just like a virus, but without the virus." What the blue hell does that even mean?<br />-A mountain lion could not kill an adult male white rhino. <br />-There are two forms of the virus. One is airborne, one is in the blood. But somehow nobody can figure out how they're related after 11 years of research, until a teenager thinks "hey, maybe one turns into the other?" This isn't even basic virology. It's common sense.<br />-11 years of advanced study and the best they can come up with is "have more babies and watch them die?"<br />-If Partial blood clots on contact with the air instantaneously, how is Samm still actively bleeding from his overnight beating when Kira walks in on him the second morning?<br />-Cutting off a hand to study virology and immunology is about as reasonable as giving someone a haircut to study their respiratory function.<br />-Viruses don't have nodules.<br />-You don't have glands inside your lungs. Also? "It looked like a gland?" Glands don't have a specific standardized appearance.<br />-Particle =/= chemical compound, or hormone, or enzyme, or pheromone. WORDS MEAN THINGS.<br />-Pheromones don't work instantaneously. It takes time for chemicals to physically cover the distance from one person to the next.<br />-You don't wear sterile gloves to perform an abdominal ultrasound.<br />-Someone having a heart attack doesn't start "thrashing and convulsing." Especially not when they're unconscious to start with.<br />-If you can't tell the difference between a virus and a pheromone, you don't belong in freshman Bio, let alone practicing medicine.<br />-A needle piercing your chest is not a "topical anesthetic." <br />-A surgical razor is not a particularly vicious or threatening weapon.<br /><br />Bottom line? If your primary plot is going to revolve around advanced virology, get someone in the field to proofread your text before setting it free into the world....</span>
  <a data-text-id="318931455737582675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_295959646" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/295959646" />
    <a title="Eric Allen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6229358-eric-allen"><img alt="Eric Allen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560117879p2/6229358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/295959646?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eric Allen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eric Allen" href="/user/show/6229358-eric-allen">Eric Allen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer295959646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6094647650834120971">Partials <br/>By Dan Wells<br/><br/>A Review by Eric Allen<br/><br/>I have been totally blown away by every single book that Dan Wells has written. I don't know where he came from all of a sudden, but in the last 4 years he's written 5 extremely good books. And as writers should, he gets better with every book that he publishes, expanding his ideas, fixing things that didn't work, and improving upon his skills as a storyteller. If you have not read I Am Not A Serial Killer yet, go buy it or check it out of the library N</span>
  <span id="freeText6094647650834120971" style="display:none">Partials <br />By Dan Wells<br /><br />A Review by Eric Allen<br /><br />I have been totally blown away by every single book that Dan Wells has written. I don't know where he came from all of a sudden, but in the last 4 years he's written 5 extremely good books. And as writers should, he gets better with every book that he publishes, expanding his ideas, fixing things that didn't work, and improving upon his skills as a storyteller. If you have not read I Am Not A Serial Killer yet, go buy it or check it out of the library NOW, you do not know what you are missing. Even if supernatural murder mystery is not your thing, it is written so well, with such an amazingly compelling character that even those who do not like the genre will be sucked into it.<br /><br />Anyway, Partials. Having finished his John Cleaver trilogy, and the suitably epic A Night of Blacker Darkness, which is only available in digital format and comes highly recomended by me if you've the means to read it, Dan Wells has started a new series with Partials. It is a far cry from his previous novels in terms of genre, instead of horror and suspense, he's tried his hand at dystopian science fiction. Where other writers tend to stumble when switching genres from their previous fare, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206043845" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Goodkind</a> comes to mind, Dan Wells has given us a spectacularly well written story in a very well crafted world, with great characters.<br /><br />Eleven years ago the Partials, genetically engineered super soldiers created by the US government rebelled. They released RM, a virus that wiped out the human race in a matter of days, leaving less than one half of one percent of the population alive with natural immunity to it. The American survivors have gathered on Long Island, ever vigilant for further Partial attacks, but none have come. They stay on their island, content to let the Partials have the rest of the world, not knowing if there are any other human survivors anywhere else in the world. <br /><br />RM still exists. It is everywhere. And in eleven years not a single baby has been born with the natural immunity to it. To ensure the future of humanity, and produce children with immunity, the Senate has introdued the Hope Act. This requires every woman of eighteen years to get pregnant as quickly as possible and stay pregnant as often as possible. Though there are some who truly believe in the Hope Act, and see it as saving humanity from extinction, most women feel that they are being treated as little better than cattle. This sentiment has given rise to the Voice, short for Voice of the People, a resistance group standing against the Senate for the human rights of not just women, but everyone.<br /><br />Enter Kira Walker, sixteen year old medic intern. She became a medic to help make a better future for humanity, and cure RM so that babies never have to die days after birth again, but is abhored by how little she is able to do. She decides that she is going to work out a cure for RM on her own, but when she analyzes a blood sample, she realizes that it really is EVERYWHERE, all around them, and even in them. This gets her to thinking that if the Partials made the virus, then they must have built a natural immunity to it into themselves. She believes that the only way to cure RM is to capture a Partial, and study it to find how their bodies repel the virus.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Her superiors refuse to allow such a dangerous mission, so with her friends Kira decides to do it on her own. Though they meet with quite a bit of disaster, they do manage to bring back one Partial alive, and though they are highly pissed at her for doing so, the Senate sees the merit in studying him. They give her five days to do her tests before they dispose of the Partial.<br /><br />Kira does her tests, and Samm, the Partial, begins to open up to her, telling her that he was part of a peace mission sent to offer a truce to the humans because they are dying out as well. Every Partial was built with an expiration date, and that date is fast approaching. She makes several discoveries, but before she can go much further, the Voice attack the hospital, almost killing her. It is deemed too dangerous to continue. Samm is set for execution, despite Kira's protests that she has almost made a breakthrough.<br /><br />Kira believes that the only way to find the cure to RM is to break Samm out, and head to the mainland to join with the Partials that seek a truce. They do so by starting a riot agaist the senate. Unfortunately, Samm was lying, and once on the mainland, Kira is taken captive. The Partials intend to use her as a test subject to find out how to remove the sterility built into their bodies so that they can begin to reproduce before their time runs out. <br /><br />As she is being tested, Kira realizes what the cure for RM is, and her friends arrive to break her out. They rush back to Long Island with the cure, hoping they are not too late to stop the remnants of humanity from tearing themselves apart in civil war. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The Good? As always Dan Wells' writing is excellent. He is great at creating characters that you can relate to, who are interesting, and for whom you want to root for. He has created a very realistic and interesting post-apocalyptic world, and he introduces it all in such a way that he never actually explains how everything works outright, which is the mark of a very good storyteller in my book. The danger of extinction feels very real as you read, and you can feel the resentment and tensions that the Hope Act creates. This book flowed along perfectly, it had its suspenseful moments, it's calm moments, and everything else in between, but nowhere did I feel as though the story dragged. Kira pretty much carries the entire story on her shoulders, but she's such a likable character that it works out well. There are some really great action scenes, but most of the story centers around Kira's inner turmoil, her inability to cure RM, her fears and apprehensions of reaching the Hope Act's pregnancy age, and her struggle to figure out what her true feelings toward her likely future husband, and it is really well done. Dan Wells is a master of inner turmoil, and he makes it not just interesting but riveting. There were also a couple very good plot twists, one of which caught me by surprise. It's not often that I don't see a plot twist coming.<br /><br />The Bad? I can only make one complaint about this book, and it's really not much of a complaint. It's more of a nitpick than anything else. Kira is a teenaged girl, and Dan Wells is not, nor has he ever been. There are a few small instances where her character seems a little off. It's hard to describe. There's a few places where she acts more like a man thinks a teenaged girl should act rather than how a teenaged girl actually would act, if that makes any sense to you. Mostly this comes out in her being a bit overly weepy, too quick to shed tears. Yes, there are women out there who will cry over just about anything, but not many of them. In my experience, women cry a lot less over trivial things than popular fiction would have us believe. Though Kira is a very strong character, she still does feel a bit more like a man's vision of a woman rather than an actual woman here and there. The instances are few and far between, but they are still there. For the most part Dan Wells does show that girls can be strong too and still remain girls, and I'm pretty sure that's what he was going for with her character.<br /><br />In conclusion this book was freaking awesome. I loved it and highly recomend it. Five stars all the way, and I highly recomend all of Dan Wells' books along with this one. If you like Partials, you should check out A Night of Darker Blackness, and I Am Not a Serial Killer. He also does a podcast called <a href="http://www.writingexcuses.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Writing Excuses</a> with a couple other authors if you are interested in getting tips from published writers on how to make your own writing better. Despite a few very minor problems that are just nitpicks, Partials was an excellent book and I cannot wait for the next in the series.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/list/6229358?shelf=read" rel="nofollow noopener"> Check out my other reviews.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6094647650834120971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer3594367643766379415"><a href='http://psilovethatbook.blogspot.co.uk' rel='nofollow noopener'>MORE? MORE! @ P.S. I love that book!</a><br/><br/>So Laura told me about this book like three years ago. Since then I have had it on my kindle as an ebook but for some absolutely unexplainable reason I never picked it up till now. I expected it also for some reason to be about a whiny girl in some advanced technology world. Do not ask me why. I do not know. So I think it rather clear that I went into this book with very low expectation, even so yes, Laura has told me it is amazing and normally I believe her. </span>
  <span id="freeText3594367643766379415" style="display:none"><a href="http://psilovethatbook.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">MORE? MORE! @ P.S. I love that book!</a><br /><br />So Laura told me about this book like three years ago. Since then I have had it on my kindle as an ebook but for some absolutely unexplainable reason I never picked it up till now. I expected it also for some reason to be about a whiny girl in some advanced technology world. Do not ask me why. I do not know. So I think it rather clear that I went into this book with very low expectation, even so yes, Laura has told me it is amazing and normally I believe her. I am weird sometimes, seriously.<br /><br />THE WORLD: The world is this book is very much dystopian. We get New York which is now a little island hosting 40,000 humans, the only survivors. Why? Because more than eleven years ago the Americans created AI (Artifical Inteligence) people to fight for them in the Isolation war against China which claimed the energy. The AI creatures were called Partials. After they won the war and came back to USA nobody knew what to do with them so they used them as easy power. If you think about it, AI is not really different from normal humans. So no surprised that Partials raised against humans and that is how eleven years ago Partials War took place. Most of the people were wiped out except for a few. By partials and then by RM virus which killed everybody who had no immunity incredibly quickly. The ones that survived are the ones living in New York Island. But that is not all, the RM did not just go away, it prevents the survival of newborns. In other world, every single child born in last eleven year died. The youngest human in the world is almost 14 years old. So the story really focuses on this little island where they have this Hope Act, by law all women after 18th birthday are mandatory to give birth to as many babies as humanly possible. The key is to find a baby which has an immunity. Statistically that is the answer. In reality, it was not working and the Senate was gonna lower the age to 16. You get the idea. Now around this little Island live outsides, people that do not agree with the Senate. But it is dangerous out there, The Voice aka the rebels are fighting the Senate about the Hope Act. But that is only half the problem. Nobody has seen a partial for eleven years. What are they doing? Where are they? Are they preparing to attack or are they just waiting till humans die out?<br /><br />CHARACTERS: The main character has a really nice name I absolutely love - Kira. She is a medic and frankly, she is a gifted researcher. I like Kira's character very very much, I like how she things and what she does. But what I loved most was how she was thinking about science. And in particularly virology. To me personally, as I am geneticist with a huge interest in virology, this part was like candy. And the best part was that there was no bullshit! What she was talking was actually scientifically correct. And the whole Lock and Key principle...brilliant! Alright so yeah, I love Kira. Now next to her we have Marcus who is her love interest. I have to agree, at first he was really annoying but then with story progressing I started to like Marcus. He is not my favorite character but he is very much an okay dude nevertheless. Aside from them there are a few more characters who play a big role in this book: Xochi, Jayden, Isorde, Haru and Madison. Well from them all my favorite was Jayden, he was a soldier but a damn damn good one. Made me cry! And my least favorite is Madison, oh my such a stupid female. Embarrassment to all women.<br /><br />And of course how could I forget Samm...oh my....*heavy breathing*. He is, yes, a partial. But boy oh boy he is good, too good I could even say. <br /><br />LOVE: So Kira had been dating Marcus since she was a child, she is 16 now. Marcus wants to get married and have children. But does Kira want that? No, what Kira wants is to find a cure to RM. So she risks her life and the existence of the left humans to get it. And in the process she meets Samm...and...and...well read it for yourself. Some things cannot be explained!<br /><br />PLUS: The whole virus things made me so interested that I read the book in one sitting. 468 pages in one evening! <br /><br />PLUS: Kira is a very good lead character. She literary was interesting all the time and I cannot think of a simple page where she annoyed me. Go Kira!<br /><br />EXTRA: Me needs the next book NOW!<br /><br /><a href="http://psilovethatbook.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">MORE? MORE! @ P.S. I love that book!</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10045234367275174610">An ARC was provided by Harpercollins Canada for review! Thank you!<br/><br/>Humans created the Partials long ago by ParaGen. They created the ultimate super being. Stronger, faster, smarter to help aid in modern warfare for the enemy hostiles. Then the Partials created the RM virus, wiping away almost the entire human population with a few being immune to the virus.<br/><br/>We find Kira, a 16 year old medical intern, who works and lives in East Meadow. She assists in the pregnancy ward of the hospital. Her best fr</span>
  <span id="freeText10045234367275174610" style="display:none">An ARC was provided by Harpercollins Canada for review! Thank you!<br /><br />Humans created the Partials long ago by ParaGen. They created the ultimate super being. Stronger, faster, smarter to help aid in modern warfare for the enemy hostiles. Then the Partials created the RM virus, wiping away almost the entire human population with a few being immune to the virus.<br /><br />We find Kira, a 16 year old medical intern, who works and lives in East Meadow. She assists in the pregnancy ward of the hospital. Her best friend Madison becomes pregnant, and knowing that the virus will kill the new born baby she sets off on a mission to help her friend and the rest of her species. Along the way she meets friends and foes and even figures out the mystery of where she came from.<br /><br />I was dying for this book and I was lucky enough to receive an ARC (THANK YOU HarperCollins! :) And boy I was not disappointed. Dan Wells writes with the pacing, tone and style set for a post-apocalyptic setting that most YA authors are writing about these days. And Mr. Wells is a great story teller. It reads like a movie. I felt like I was right there as one of the characters walking in East Meadow making do with what I had after 99.996% of the human population had been decimated.<br /><br />Yes the book starts of slow, but what after reading more and more, your mind is set into Kira’s world where things aren’t what they seem to be. This book ends on a cliffhanger so I am warning you, you will get frustrated! I know I was!<br /><br />This book is chock full of mystery, suspense action and a tinge of romance.</span>

<div id="review_292113766" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/292113766" />
    <a title="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva"><img alt="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392555495p2/1491042.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/292113766?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" href="/user/show/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva">Aly (Fantasy4eva)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=my-kinda-protagonist">my-kinda-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=received-for-review">received-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=fast-paced-and-engrossing">fast-paced-and-engrossing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=pleasantly-surprised">pleasantly-surprised</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=digging-the-premise">digging-the-premise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=boys-that-make-me-swoon">boys-that-make-me-swoon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=had-me-at-hello">had-me-at-hello</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=lets-be-mates">lets-be-mates</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer292113766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9182826438740042496">Dude. How <i>cool</i> is this book!<br/><br/>Fighting, saving the wold, kick-ass protagonist and mates that completely have your back, grenades, going on dangerous and not- so- sophisticated adventures, loyal and brave. Oh and very likable.<br/><br/>Kira! A protagonist that I liked a lot. It really is a great feeling to find yourself genuinely liking the protagonist. We so need more of those.<br/><br/>Our gal is brave, a heart-breaker (tut tut), tough, loyal and caring. Being a medic is in her blood. I say this because even when th</span>
  <span id="freeText9182826438740042496" style="display:none">Dude. How <i>cool</i> is this book!<br /><br />Fighting, saving the wold, kick-ass protagonist and mates that completely have your back, grenades, going on dangerous and not- so- sophisticated adventures, loyal and brave. Oh and very likable.<br /><br />Kira! A protagonist that I liked a lot. It really is a great feeling to find yourself genuinely liking the protagonist. We so need more of those.<br /><br />Our gal is brave, a heart-breaker (tut tut), tough, loyal and caring. Being a medic is in her blood. I say this because even when the enemy is hurt - she's the first to let her group know that she can't leave them behind, that they need help. And it's great to see. Because often when people start dying, the story focuses on moving along and you're kind of left like. Urmm, so is nobody going to even act like they care right now? But Kira cared.<br /><br />Kira has been with Marcus for years. And ever since the partials released the virus, every child that is born, dies. The government is becoming desperate and are considering decreasing the age to 16 in the 'Hope Act'. What this means is that -if this law is passed- that instead of 18, every woman have to get pregnant by 16. On top of it all, the rebel group 'Voice' are becoming more and more violent. So when Kira's best mate gets pregnant, she is determined to find the answer to save her baby. Even if she has to go into partial territory and bring back one with her. But it's when she comes across a partial does her way of thinking start to change. You see, this partial looks more human than she would like, he has a name, a voice, and shows feelings. He also shares a very different story to what they have been led to believe.<br /><br />What is a girl to do?<br /><br />What I loved about her was that she was no helpless girl in distress. She didn't rely on others. She was thorough, practical and got the job done. But she wasn't heartless. She's loyal and brave, but not only just towards her people.<br /><br />Does she string Marcus along: seemes like it often. That was one of my gripes. (Another was all the info dumping throughout the book. It did tend to get a bit too much at times) I mean, do you guys think she loves him? I sure don't. Do I hold a grudge against her for being a bitch to him? (even if it is not intentionally). As much as I felt sorry for the guy, the answer is no. Because it's kinda refreshing to read about a girl who puts something else first before a guy. Who doesn't lose all common sense when he comes into her vicinity. Sorry, but I like this badass chick. MORE PLEASE. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He was a nice lad. A little boring to be frank. But still a nice guy. I think she should have just been up-front from the get-go rather than giving him hope throughout. That bothered me <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This book is action packed, intense and has a complete different vibe to every other book I've read in this genre -which is something, because right now they're all starting to seem pretty similar to me!. It's completely wonderful to ease into. I knew I was onto something great a few pages in. Also, it's no small book. The length can be daunting, but I devoured PARTIALS. So do not even worry your pretty little heads off about the size of the book, trust me.<br /><br />PARTIALS also features a great cast. You have these mates, or relatives of mates that come together basically for one common cause. I just find it a bit meh that they all decided upon it because the person was closer to home. Although, I guess I could just look at the bigger picture and let them off. From Marcus, Jayden, Xochi, Isolde, Haru and Madison: they all won me over. Did I get to know them as much as I would have liked? No. But they made a strong impression, and I think that's good enough for the first book. I cared about them and rooted for them all. Although Haru was quite trying. Perhaps not my kind of guy since he often acted like a tool and a robot, but I know his heart was in the right place. I'm just not sure If he'll grow on me the way he's going. The guy has a major chip on his shoulder.<br /><br />Did I have a favourite. Oh definitely, although I do feel his potential wasn't played up on as much as it could have been. Often he wasn't there, or I felt like his character potential was held back. And that's definitely Jayden. Not only did he make me swoon, but I also loved how he was such a natural leader - yet also knew when he needed to back down for the greater good. Sure, he has the tendency to act tough, but you can see that underneath it all he has such a soft spot for his mates. He would do anything for them and more. He definitely proved himself to me.<br /><br /><b>Question for those who have read the book!</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[OMG THE END. WHYYY. Feel so gutted. Why is it always the cool, awesome guy that dies. So annoyed right now :/. Is it me or did any of you get the gist that Jayden really liked Kira. I mean, I got that impression at first, but then things got muddled as they separated and as she started to have Samm and Marcus drama. But what he does toward the end, saving her like that - when he didn't have to. Like surely it was more than just liking, right. Might be pulling it a stretch (BUT) maybe he even loved her :(( * sniffs* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="9182826438740042496" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/305468249" />
    <a title="Ava" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5832186-ava"><img alt="Ava" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/305468249?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ava" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ava" href="/user/show/5832186-ava">Ava</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=paranormal-romance-fiction">paranormal-romance-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=science-fiction-romance">science-fiction-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=contains-boyfriend">contains-boyfriend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=four-stars">four-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer305468249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4948749907619813034">Oh, man. This book made me feel like humanity was my nasty ex, and I had just dumped his ass before snapping my fingers in Z-formation.<br/><br/>By that, I mean most of the humans in this book pissed me off - though they were supposed to. <br/><br/>PARTIALS takes place in a futuristic world where humanity is quickly going extinct after a virus released during the Partial-Human war kills off babies less than a week after birth. Kira Walker, sixteen, is a medic-in-training. When someone important to her becomes pregn</span>
  <span id="freeText4948749907619813034" style="display:none">Oh, man. This book made me feel like humanity was my nasty ex, and I had just dumped his ass before snapping my fingers in Z-formation.<br /><br />By that, I mean most of the humans in this book pissed me off - though they were supposed to. <br /><br />PARTIALS takes place in a futuristic world where humanity is quickly going extinct after a virus released during the Partial-Human war kills off babies less than a week after birth. Kira Walker, sixteen, is a medic-in-training. When someone important to her becomes pregnant, she resolves to find a Partial, experiment on it, and try to save the human race. But there’s more background to the war and the Partials than she initially thought, and what she discovers will turn her world upside down. <br /><br />That was about the shittiest blurb I’ve ever written<s> but GIVE ME A BREAK OKAY AND THIS WILL BE A MINI REVIEW BECAUSE I’M TIRED.</s><br /><br />The world-building and plot was amazing, hands-down. It was extremely immersive, and even though I didn’t understand a lot of the medical talk being the idiot that I am, I still appreciated the effort Wells put into it. It was very, well, scientific.<br /><br />The politics and government in PARTIALS was brilliant, and this book made me feel like humanity was my nasty ex, and I had just dumped his ass before snapping my fingers in Z-formation. I mean, TEAM NATURE, Y'ALL.<br /><br />By that, I mean I was cheering when I read about the flora and fauna taking over the cities.<br /><br />I didn’t like most of the characters, Samm the Partial being an exception. I loved how sweet and mysterious he was without being a huge jerk. While Kira was a determined badass, she was also boneheaded and whiny. Her friends annoyed the crap out of me, particularly Madison and Marcus, her boyfriend.<br /><br />There wasn’t a lot of romance in PARTIALS, though when there was, it was with Marcus, Kira’s boyfriend. Not Samm. Unfortunately.<br /><br /><s>YOU CAN HEAR ME GROANING FROM HERE</s><br /><br />The writing was average for me, honestly. Some people didn’t care for it and others couldn’t get enough, but I found it to be alright.<br /><br />PARTIALS didn’t consume me as much as I thought it would, being a predictable read and all, but it was good anyway.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4948749907619813034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('I/aPDyRC3cuIB98Ex9O6sCWFFuzldnviOr4He3E48zWlStt8MsMFO/9tISq6uNCakmX7LYyBDjaR9sWDUZhXAA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AWFMmXf1jlOE9a24Gk1rG8D1Pkf/bjE8wnA45hyIUFKH3RjqYXRWo/OfU5ZnJgExdxXThpaZROhpOPoePCj0Zw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8435180147585179133">Dan Wells is a thriller and science fiction writer. Born in Utah, he spent his early years reading and writing. He is he author of the Partials series (Partials, Isolation, Fragments, and Ruins), the John Cleaver series (I Am Not a Serial Killer, Mr. Monster, and I Don't Want To Kill You), and a few others (The Hollow City, A Night of Blacker Darkness, etc). He was a Campbell nomine for best new w</span>
  <span id="freeText8435180147585179133" style="display:none">Dan Wells is a thriller and science fiction writer. Born in Utah, he spent his early years reading and writing. He is he author of the Partials series (Partials, Isolation, Fragments, and Ruins), the John Cleaver series (I Am Not a Serial Killer, Mr. Monster, and I Don't Want To Kill You), and a few others (The Hollow City, A Night of Blacker Darkness, etc). He was a Campbell nomine for best new writer, and has won a Hugo award for his work on the podcast Writing Excuses; the podcast is also a multiple winner of the Parsec Award.</span>
